Current Commentary

The Inherent Contradictions of Japanese Imperialism in its Aggression Against China 11

All changes in history are undeniably governed by economic conditions, and the path of national struggles changes its methods in accordance with changes in economic conditions, like a shadow following a form, inextricably linked. National struggles before the eighteenth century were struggles under the feudal system. Production under the feudal system took land as its primary element, so the methods of its national struggles also centered on the issue of land. The motivation behind the aggression of strong nations against weak nations often stemmed from population growth and the resulting insufficient production. Their actions often involved nothing more than seizing territory, attacking cities, enslaving people, and engaging in outrageous extortion. Since the Industrial Revolution, technological innovations have emerged day by day. The national struggles arising from the insufficient production of the feudal era have also gradually transformed their methods into a competition for consumer markets. The purpose of all conflicts between capitalist powers and the aggression of powers against weak nations lies in acquiring a backward nation in production to absorb their surplus products. Even after the European War, there were indeed some territorial changes, but the intention was still nothing more than the division of colonies and the transfer of ports. While also supporting small nations to maintain military superiority, the central issue remained the establishment of their economic hegemony, organizing their lines of exploiting weak nations with surplus products.

Japanese imperialism's aggression against China is, of course, no exception. The motive behind this aggression against China stems from economic panic, and the economic panic stems from overproduction. If the goal of invading to resolve overproduction is its driving force, then its primary purpose is to monopolize the consumer market in the three northeastern provinces. It is very obvious that the inherent contradictions of capitalism are naturally becoming increasingly acute, so all actions arising from these contradictions will inevitably fall into contradiction or be an unavoidable result. Since the September 18th Incident, the decline of Japanese imperialism's trade with China has been an undeniable fact. This is partly due to the anti-Japanese movement by the people of the country, and partly due to the natural decline in purchasing power in the aftermath of war and turmoil. Although the Japanese boast about the progress of trade with Japan in the three northeastern provinces, according to our understanding, some of the Japanese goods imported into the Northeast are an increase in Japanese merchants' inventory, and even more are materials for Japanese construction and military equipment in Manchukuo. In reality, consumers belonging to the people are likely decreasing rather than increasing. If one were to say that the power of iron hooves and bullets can increase the purchasing power of the Chinese people, then how could this be true? Therefore, for the past year and a half, Japanese imperialism's aggression against China has only destroyed China's consumer market, causing the state of overproduction among Japanese imperialism and the powers to continue to increase. The contradictions of the entire capitalism system are becoming increasingly acute. What Japanese imperialism seeks in its aggression against China is the opposite of what it gets.

If the Japanese must comfort themselves with the thought that their invasion has not yet been completed, then may I ask, what will happen when the invasion is indeed completed? Manchuria and Mongolia are what the Japanese regard as resources. If the Japanese were to succeed in the three northeastern provinces, then their greatest hope would naturally be to develop the industries of Manchuria and Mongolia as stated in the Tanaka Memorial. If this were indeed the case, then the inherent contradictions of Japanese imperialism would certainly leap forward to an irreparable extent. Since the current economic panic is a high degree of overproduction, then the result of developing the resources of Manchuria and Mongolia and increasing the state of overproduction would not add another great driving force? Would the route of economic panic not sink even further into an abyss for all time? What kind of power will the Japanese use at that time to absorb this unprecedented surplus of products? Regarding this point, we do not wish to use subjective prejudices to make self-deceiving quick remarks. Rather, based on the facts, the Japanese bourgeoisie is deeply afraid that after the development of Manchuria and Mongolia, most of the industries in the Japanese mainland will be defeated due to insufficient competition. Therefore, if the result of Japanese imperialism's development of Manchuria and Mongolia is that Manchurian and Mongolian products are sufficient to supply the needs of Manchuria and Mongolia and the Chinese mainland, then it would be a major contradiction with the European and American powers, and the contradiction with the Japanese mainland would be impossible to resolve.

Whether successful or unsuccessful, Japanese imperialism's aggression against China only increases its inherent contradictions and cannot resolve its current panic, as described above. Therefore, those who hope for a compromise may use this to flaunt their cleverness in enduring humiliation. However, we must state here that Japanese imperialism's aggression against China arises from the inherent contradictions of the entire capitalism. The result of the aggression is sufficient to make the contradictions of Chinese society rapidly become acute. The environment of the times is conducive to the completion of the objective conditions for China's anti-imperialist national revolution. Therefore, the theory of compromise only prolongs the time of Japanese imperialism's final struggle, placing itself in the ranks of the objects of the revolution, and compromise will ultimately fail to achieve its aim of escaping the environment where interests are concerned. This is something that the people of the country must understand.

Xifengkou

Enemy Retreats to the Vicinity of Pingquan 12

Liu's Division Advances Towards Shouwangfen and Other Places

Japanese Army at Gubeikou Also Takes No Active Action

(Tianjin) A telegram from Zunhua states that the enemy forces outside Xifengkou have retreated seventy or eighty li, concentrating in the Shouwangfen Kuancheng area, north of Pingquan, waiting for reinforcements. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) A telegram from Kaiping states that after suffering setbacks outside Lengkou, the enemy had not attacked again as of the evening of the 28th. They bomb us daily with artillery and planes. At night, our army uses various methods to harass the enemy. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Luo Zhou) At the Lengkou front, the enemy launched a night attack on the Shanshen Temple position on the right flank of our 囗 division at 1:00 AM on the 29th, launching several assaults, all of which were repulsed by us. Many documents were found among the bodies of the enemy killed, and are being studied in the division headquarters. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan and Xiong Xiling are now at the Luowenyu battlefield, rescuing wounded soldiers. The Red Swastika Society rescue team is departing for Lengkou today. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) At the Luowenyu front, after the enemy army was repulsed by us, they are currently retreating along the main road from Luowenyu to Chengde, stopping at Shouwangfen Liuhe, about eighty or ninety li from Luowenyu, and are actively building fortifications. Our Liu Ruming Division has arrived at Banbishan. In addition to ordering its subordinates to deploy tightly, it has also sent a cavalry unit to advance towards Shouwangfen. The enemy soldiers at Banbishan were surrounded and fiercely attacked by our Dong Regiment and Wang Brigade and have retreated to Liuhe, where they are actively constructing fortifications. When the enemy attacked Banbishan, they committed atrocities such as rape, plunder, and looting, and even raped three women from good families and killed more than ten innocent people. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) After the enemy at Banbishan was repulsed by us, they constructed fortifications at Liuhe and Shouwangfen. Our Liu Ruming Division has deployed a tight defense at Banbishan and sent cavalry to advance towards Shouwangfen. The enemy airfield at Datun was attacked at night by the people and our plainclothes troops, and five or six enemy planes were burned. Yesterday afternoon, several dozen enemy plainclothes troops harassed Xifengkou and were repulsed by our guerrillas. Yesterday, we launched an attack from the Great Wall pass between Dongjiakou and Tiemen, encountering the enemy near Gushan, wounding hundreds of them, and burning several cargo vehicles. Our side suffered several dozen casualties. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan telegraphed Peiping, stating that after the enemy at Luowenyu retreated to Kuancheng and Pingquan, only plainclothes troops were left on the front line to move back and forth. Our army has partially advanced forward, with the majority awaiting orders to advance. Furthermore, the enemy who retreated from the Great Wall has moved towards Fengning, and there is indeed fighting in Fengning. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Wang Yizhe concluded his discussions with important officials in Peiping and returned to his post this morning. The enemy at Gubeikou, affected by the fighting in Fengning, is preparing to retreat and provide support. Enemy planes occasionally bomb Shixia in Miyun, but our side's losses are not severe. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telephone call from Shixia Town reports that at 9:00 AM this morning, seven enemy planes flew to the Sanjiangkou west of Shixia and dropped two bombs, injuring two camel drivers. A certain regiment of a certain division stationed at Simatai exited the pass over twenty li this morning but did not find the enemy. The Japanese have set up over a hundred wooden figures dressed as Japanese at the south gate of Gubeikou, for unknown reasons. Refugees at Gubeikou were machine-gunned by the enemy, resulting in many deaths and injuries, and many women were stripped of their lower garments. (29th Special Dispatch)

Enemy Army Attacked at Panjiakou, Ambushed 13

(Beiping) Zhao Brigade's Platoon Leader Li, at approximately 2:00 AM on the 28th, led over ten members of a courageous team in an ambush near the west gate of Panjiakou Lanqi. At approximately 7:00 AM, the enemy attacked from the east of the river, but we discovered them and fired fiercely with automatic rifles, killing over ten enemy soldiers and seizing twelve machine guns. The enemy then collapsed and scattered. (29th Special Dispatch)

A Glimpse of the Japanese Army's Inhumanity 14

(Tianjin) After the enemy retreated at Luowen, our Division Commander Liu Ruming sent troops to clear the battlefield. From the body of Sato Yoshio, a squad leader of the 31st Battalion of enemy soldiers killed in action, a diary was found containing a diary entry from March 2 stating that while camping en route from Chaoyang to Lingyuan, because residents were spreading anti-propaganda, all residents in that area, regardless of gender or age, were killed and expelled without exception. The inhumanity of the Japanese is heartbreaking and is a great shame for our country. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Due to repeated defeats and excessive numbers of wounded soldiers, the enemy seized civilian laborers to carry them. Near Mozidi, the civilian laborers killed over ten escorting soldiers and abandoned the wounded soldiers on the ground. After the enemy soldiers discovered this, they massacred all the residents in the nearby village. (29th Special Dispatch)

Shang Zhen's Telegram Replies to Chairman Chiang 15

(Nanjing) Chiang Kai-shek, due to Shang Zhen's bravery in resisting the enemy, sent a telegram to comfort and encourage him and to indicate the next steps. Shang recently replied to Chiang, stating that since the enemy made contact with us on the 21st, considering that the terrain near Lengkou was poor and difficult to defend, he resolved to engage the enemy near Xiaojiayingzi, thirty li outside the pass. For the past four days, the enemy has been unable to advance a single step. However, according to reports from all sides, the enemy seems determined to capture Lengkou and has dispatched four support teams with the 囗 regiment as the core, attached with cavalry and artillery, advancing towards us along different routes. Zhen does not consider the possibility of success or failure, but is determined to fight them to the end. He inspected the front line yesterday, and morale is still strong, which is a great comfort to those far away. (29th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Army Continues to Depart for Jehol 16

(Beiping) All of the Japanese 16th Division is departing from Japan for Jehol. The advanced units have already arrived in Jehol. Part of its 14th Division, which was left in Japan, is also departing Japan for Jehol. It is heard that more of their troops are preparing to be mobilized. Since Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations and is determined to expand the war, it is feared that subsequent troops will continue to arrive. (29th Telegram)

People of Pingquan and Kuancheng Resist the Enemy 17

(Beiping) A telegram from Zunhua on the 28th states that the enemy outside Dongjiakou Duofangzi and the enemy outside Tiemenguan have been fiercely attacked by our army and harassed in their rear by our plainclothes troops in recent days. On the afternoon of the 27th, they all retreated towards Pingquan. After the Japanese entered Jehol, they committed rape, plunder, and murder everywhere. Villages outside the pass have been mostly burned down. The people in the Pingquan and Kuancheng areas have risen up to resist. Kuancheng has been burned down. There are still a small number of very embarrassed enemy soldiers outside Xifengkou. The enemy who collapsed at Luowenyu passed by Baimachuan on the evening of the 27th, and many military supplies were seized. (28th Special Dispatch)

Luowenyu Area Suffers Devastation 18

(Beiping) A telegram from Zunhua on the 28th states that Song Zheyuan said that after the Japanese occupied Luowenyu, they carried out wanton devastation. After being repulsed by us, local gentry Lu Guangping and others wept and complained about the Japanese army's atrocities. Food and furniture were looted, and the elderly, young, and women were all raped. Over eighty people, including Qiang Gu Ma Yongle Changchuan were shot and killed. The militia and police all held the determination to fight the enemy to the death and avenge this great shame. (28th Telegram)

A Certain Military Officer of the Righteous Army Speaks 19

(Beiping) A high-ranking military officer from Zheng Guilin's unit of the Righteous Army came to Beiping on official business. According to his account, at dawn on the 27th, the puppet troops of Li Jichun, Zhao [name missing], Zi Bin and others, along with a joint Japanese force, totaling more than 2,000 infantry, over 200 cavalry, carrying more than ten cannons and over twenty machine guns, advanced from the direction of Yiyuan Pass towards our army's positions at Xiaoxue Gou, Zaishan Yu Kou and other locations. At the same time, two aircraft were dispatched to assist in bombing our army. Our army then sent the 囗th and 囗th echelons to deliver a head-on blow, and dispatched the 囗th and 囗th brigades to bypass Yiyuan Pass from Baishanpo Zhangzhuang, attacking their rear. The enemy failed to succeed and retreated to Yiyuan Pass. Our army did not pursue due to a lack of ammunition. In this battle, more than thirty enemies were killed, and more than twenty guns were captured. Our army also suffered thirty casualties. The wounded soldiers have been sent to the rear hospital of the First Army Corps of North China in Tianjin. Our army's position is currently still firmly held at Wangzhuang Suzhuang. (29th Dispatch)

Memorial Service for Revolutionary Martyrs

Wang Zhaoming Speaks on His Thoughts on the Memorial of Revolutionary Martyrs 20

Strive Forward with a Spirit of Sacrifice

We Should Emulate Them to Complete the Revolution

(Nanjing) The Central Committee held a memorial service for revolutionary martyrs at 8 AM on the 29th. Lin Sen, Wang Zhaoming, Ye Chucang, and others attended. Ye Chucang presided over the meeting. Wang Zhaoming gave a report, the original text of which is as follows:

"Comrades, the revolutionary battle of March 29th is the most tragic page in the history of our Chinese revolution, and at the same time, it is also the most glorious page in the history of our Chinese revolution. Every year on this day, comrades of our party hold memorial services to commemorate this most tragic and most glorious historical event of the revolution. When we commemorate, if we ask a comrade to make a report and completely report the content, I am afraid it is impossible to do so in a short time. Generally, we have countless feelings every time we commemorate. Now I can only bring up one point of the feelings and share it with you. Before March 29th, most revolutionary comrades already knew that the uprising on March 29th would definitely fail. We only need to read Mr. Huang Keqiang's report to know that several important conditions were completely lost. First, we must ensure that the enemy does not know our news before the uprising, but according to Mr. Huang Keqiang's report, the enemy already knew our news before March 29th. This is one point. Second, we see in Mr. Huang Keqiang's report that comrades from various places who were rising up cannot gather in Guangzhou and are being hindered and monitored everywhere. Therefore, before March 29th, Mr. Huang Keqiang and other comrades knew that these two important conditions for the success of the revolution had been lost and expected that this revolution would definitely fail.

But since the comrades at that time clearly knew that this revolution was going to fail, why did they still do the March 29th event? This is clearly stated in the report at the time. One passage says, "Comrades in Nanyang donated a lot of funds to support the revolution. If they did not proceed due to the leakage of the opportunity at that time, how could they be worthy of the comrades in Nanyang, and they could no longer raise funds from them. Therefore, regardless of success or failure, they decided to start the uprising on March 29th." But how much money was raised at that time? The total amount was only 100,000 yuan, and as for those who sacrificed for this revolution, there were as many as seventy-two well-known people, all of whom were the elite of our party and the talents of the country. Why were they so clear about the failure, but still did it? The first answer is that the revolutionaries have a spirit of sacrifice, but where does this spirit of sacrifice come from? The second answer is probably different for everyone. In my humble opinion, every revolutionary must have a certain concept. He does his best for the revolution and knows that the revolution will definitely succeed, but it does not necessarily have to be achieved in his lifetime. As long as he can do a little bit to reach the road to success before the revolution succeeds, that is his lifelong responsibility. This is the source of his spirit of sacrifice.

To use road construction as a metaphor, to know that to build a wide and smooth road, countless small stones must first be used to fill it. The countless flesh and blood of us revolutionaries are these countless small stones. Only with the countless flesh and blood of us to do the filling work can the revolutionary road be completed. Therefore, revolutionaries only pay attention to the success of the revolution and do not care about their own success. If every revolutionary can do this, then the vitality of the revolution will continue and eventually lead to success. No matter what kind of environment is changed, or what kind of twists and turns are experienced, as long as the vitality continues, then generations of young people will continue to do the revolutionary cause, and the revolutionary cause will become more and more upward and more and more expanded. From March 29th of Xinhai until today, it has been more than twenty years. During these twenty years, China has indeed undergone many changes, and even now the work of the revolution has encountered great obstacles, but in terms of revolutionary power, it is much greater than in Xinhai. During these twenty years, has the vitality of the Chinese revolution been cut off? No, it has not been cut off. Since it has not been cut off, then we should emulate the spirit of sacrifice of the martyrs, identify the direction, and complete this revolutionary road. If our direction is correct, we should not have a temporary success mentality, but should move forward bravely, and use countless hot blood to form this road to success. Even if the first batch of people does not succeed, the second batch of people will continue to do it. If the second batch of people does not succeed, then the third, fourth, fifth, and sixth batches of people will continue to do it. As long as the direction of the revolution is correct and the vitality of the revolution is not cut off, the success of the revolution will eventually come. Today, when we commemorate the revolutionary martyrs, it is as if the revolutionary martyrs are standing in front of us, leading us to continue to move forward. Therefore, since we comrades have assumed the mission of the revolution, we should strive forward, so that our courage will not disappear, the vitality of the revolution will not be interrupted, and we can finally achieve our goal. The road of revolution has been opened for us by the martyrs. We who die later continue to fill this road with our flesh and blood, and work together to seek the final success, so that we will not fail the sacrifices of the Premier and the general martyrs." (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Held in Various Places

Commemoration of Revolutionary Martyrs 21

(Nanjing) The 29th is the commemoration of the Yellow Flower Mound Martyrs. The city of Nanjing flew flags at half-mast and suspended entertainment and banquets to express condolences. More than 300 representatives from all walks of life held a memorial meeting at the city party headquarters at 9 AM, presided over by Zhang Yuanliang, who reported on the course of the martyrs' sacrifice in the March 29th Incident and their spirit of sacrifice for the country. At this time when the Northeast has fallen and the violent Japanese are advancing, we should emulate the martyrs' spirit of sacrifice and struggle, and unite to resist the insults, so as not to be ashamed of the meaning of commemorating the martyrs. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Municipal Government held a memorial service for revolutionary martyrs on the 29th. All staff members attended, presided over by Secretary-General Lai Lian, who reported that they should emulate the spirit of sacrifice of the revolutionary martyrs and rise up together to avenge the national and ethnic humiliation. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Jinan) Today, the whole city flew flags at half-mast and suspended entertainment. The provincial party headquarters convened representatives from various counties to hold a memorial meeting. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Changsha) At 9 AM on the 29th, the Provincial Party Rectification Committee convened people from all walks of life to hold a Yellow Flower Mound memorial meeting. The whole city flew flags at half-mast and suspended entertainment. (29th Special Dispatch)

Page 8

League of Nations Advisory Committee 23

Met for Two Hours Without Special Developments

Adjourned Until After Easter

(Geneva) The Advisory Committee of the League of Nations, organized to monitor the Sino-Japanese dispute, has now read the notification of Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations and Secretary-General Drummond's reply. The Advisory Committee has not yet decided to issue a new statement to criticize Japan's views stated in the Japanese notification. However, the committee intends to promptly study various issues arising from the non-recognition of "Manchukuo." In addition, the representatives of various countries in the committee will also seek the opinions of their respective governments on the prohibition of the transportation of arms to belligerent countries. According to reports, the various issues arising from the non-recognition of "Manchukuo" include "Manchukuo's" request to join the International Postal and Telegraph Union and the status of consuls of various countries stationed in Manchuria vis-à-vis local officials. (28th Havas Dispatch)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Advisory Committee met at 5:30 tonight and adjourned at 7:15. At the time of adjournment, the date of the next meeting was not decided, but it may not be held again before Easter. The Advisory Committee discussed the general situation arising from Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, but decided not to reply. The Irish representative, Lester, first raised the issue of Japan's withdrawal, saying that he knew that this matter was only indirectly related to the Advisory Committee, but he felt that the Advisory Committee might as well take a stand and reply to Japan's notification of withdrawal. The reply should point out that although Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, it is still bound by Article 10 of the Covenant. The reply should also refute the claim in the Japanese document to the Secretariat that Japan has the right to independently interpret international treaties concerning the relationship between Japan and other countries. There was some discussion on this point, but it was finally decided that since the various sections of the Japanese document had already been replied to by the Secretariat, the Advisory Committee did not need to reply. The Advisory Committee then listened to a report by the League of Nations Deputy Secretary-General, Italian Biruti, on the issue of non-recognition of "Manchukuo." The report stated what actions should be taken regarding "Manchukuo's" request to join the Postal Union, and how to treat "Manchukuo's" stamps, coins, passports, and other items. This report is not yet complete and will be submitted to the subcommittee specializing in the non-recognition of "Manchukuo." This committee will convene a meeting after Easter. The Advisory Committee then discussed the issue of arms embargo in order to prepare the agenda for the embargo committee. However, the general opinion was that the attitude of a certain major country towards this matter was still uncertain, so there was nothing to do about this matter at present. It was felt that it was appropriate to wait a little longer to see the results of the arms embargo proposal related to the dispute with the two South American countries. The Czech representative, Jiseski (Czech Minister to Switzerland), made very clear remarks and asked about the United States' attitude towards this matter, but the American representative, Wilson, attended as an observer and remained silent throughout, neither participating in the discussion nor expressing the opinion of his government. Therefore, the date of the embargo committee meeting has not been set, but it will probably have to wait until after Easter. Today, only twenty-one countries attended the meeting, including the United States. The Turkish representative did not attend. The British representative was the Secretary of the Foreign Office, Kail. France was represented by Masigli. The German representative was Kaina. (28th Reuters Dispatch)

US House Foreign Affairs Committee

Passes Arms Embargo 24

The Bill Seems Likely to Pass Soon

(Washington) The bill authorizing the US President to order an arms embargo has been passed by the House Foreign Affairs Committee today, and it seems likely to pass soon. What the House Foreign Affairs Committee passed was to authorize the President to order an embargo without consulting other countries. There is still some doubt as to whether the Senate will approve such broad powers in the future. The driving force behind this bill is entirely the situation in South America, because at present the US President can only order an embargo of arms to countries in civil unrest, and has no right to order an embargo to belligerent countries. At a time when trade between the United States and South America has declined year after year, members of Congress believe that the first step to restoring commerce in Latin America is to stop the war between Bolivia and Paraguay and Colombia, so that their funds for purchasing arms can be used to improve business routes and pay off public debt interest. This is why they are eager to embargo arms to belligerent countries in South America. (28th National Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, there is currently no consensus on the international level regarding the embargo of arms to belligerent countries since the British government voluntarily abandoned it. The League of Nations Advisory Committee also did not have a specific resolution at its meeting on the 28th. The US House of Representatives Foreign Affairs Committee passed a motion authorizing the President to handle this matter by a vote of sixteen to fifteen on the 28th. The development of this case is of utmost importance to the United States, as all countries are clearly looking to the United States for guidance on this matter. If President Roosevelt expresses something after being authorized by Congress, the League of Nations will have a unified action. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Japan Withdraws from the League of Nations

Is This Really the Inside Story? 25

(Geneva) Our representative obtained information from the League of Nations that the Japanese government will not only continue to cooperate with various agencies of the League of Nations other than the Administrative Council and the General Assembly, but is also prepared to have Japanese representatives participate in all committees of the League of Nations. An organizational method is currently being studied to ensure that all agencies of the League of Nations in Geneva have Japanese diplomats and experts. It is rumored that the number of Japanese personnel in the League of Nations will be even greater than before the announcement of withdrawal. (29th Havas Dispatch)

Japanese Government Decides to Establish

Naval Department in Changchun 28

(Tokyo) In order to facilitate liaison with "Manchukuo," the Navy has decided to establish a naval department stationed in Changchun. Prince Fushimi has requested the Emperor's approval and obtained his approval. The official announcement was made today in the official gazette. (29th Electric Communication Agency Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The newly established naval department stationed in Manchukuo is equivalent to a naval base department and is responsible for defending the coasts and rivers of Manchukuo. It is directly under the Emperor and commands subordinate warships and troops. A commander is appointed, who is subject to the control of the Minister of the Navy and is in charge of military and political affairs. Under him are a chief of staff, staff officers, adjutants, chief engineer, and chief accountant. The appointments will be announced on April 1. The position of commander will be held by Major General Kobayashi Shōzaburō, the current chief officer of the special naval organization in Manchukuo. The chief of staff will be held by Colonel Itō Seiichi, the second-ranking officer. (29th Electric Communication Agency Dispatch)

Second Batch Departure Date 29

Harbin Far East Bank

Borrows Money from Japanese Banks 30

(Tokyo) According to today's Tokyo Nichi Nichi Shimbun, the president of the Harbin Far East Bank, Xiyabiro, who came to Tokyo last time, has been negotiating with the authorities of the Bank of Korea on Russo-Japanese economic issues for several days. He completed his mission and left Tokyo on the 27th. It is reported that his mission was quite important. In addition to borrowing 10 million yuan from the Bank of Korea, there are various proposals regarding financial cooperation between the two countries, namely, the Russian side will lend 30 million yuan from the Bank of Korea for Russian economic institutions and enterprises in the North Manchuria region, using the Far East Bank banknotes. Therefore, a branch of the Far East Bank will be opened in Tokyo, and the restoration of the Bank of Korea branch in Vladivostok will be a condition for exchange. The Bank of Korea authorities are carefully considering this and will have concrete discussions when President Kato visits Manchuria next month. (29th Electric Communication Agency Dispatch)

Matsuoka Yōsuke

Utters More Mad Words Slandering Us 31

(New York) Last night, the Japanese representative to the League of Nations, Matsuoka Yōsuke, was invited to a banquet by the New York Japanese Chamber of Commerce. During the speech, he praised the United States, saying, "We have been striving in Geneva to make the Western countries understand the difficulties of Japan's current situation, but to no avail. Japan is a small country, located between the two major countries of China and Russia. Both of these major countries are in revolution, which is enough to worry Japan. China is surrounded by bandits, disasters, and poverty. The main cause of the turmoil in the Far East is the chaos in China. China does not recognize international obligations, which harms Japan. China has no ability to defend itself, because China is not a country but a group of various peoples. Japan has proposed to cooperate with China to seek peace and prosperity in Manchuria, but this proposal has always been opposed by China, especially after the Kuomintang came to power." He also said that the League of Nations has no ability to solve the China problem. (29th Havas Dispatch)

Chiang Kai-shek, Wang Zhaoming, Lin Sen, Yu Youren, Dai Chuanxian, Sun Ke, Gu Mengyu, Ju Zheng, Chen Yaofu, Li Liejun, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Gongbo, Chen Bijun, Chu Minyi, Zhu Peide, Kong Xiangxi, Zhang Qun, Ma Chaojun, Gu Zhutong, Chen Bulei, Jing Hengyi, Shi Ying, Shi Qingyang, Chen Ce, Tang Shengzhi, He Yaozu, Wu Tiecheng, Jiang Zuobin, Zhou Fohai, Zeng Zhongming, Duan Xipeng, Huang Fusheng, Ran Hancao, Shao Lizi, Jiao Yitang, Li Ciwen, Huang Jichen, Zhou Qigang, Chen Zhaoying, Chen Shuren, Ding Chaowu, Wang Qi, Zhang Daofan, Mao Zuquan, Yu Jingtang, Tang Youren, Wang Luyi, Xiao Jishan, Gu Zhenggang, Bai Yunti, Hong Ludong, Deng Jiayan, and more than 50 other people attended. (3) Dai Chuanxian and six other members proposed to temporarily conclude the Capital Construction Committee and transfer the original funds to build compulsory primary schools in the city of Beijing. The resolution was approved. The Capital Construction Committee is limited to conclude by the end of April. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Wang Jingwei has resumed his duties. On the morning of the 30th, after the Standing Committee approved the resumption of duties case, he immediately returned to the Executive Yuan in the afternoon to resume his duties. The Secretariat has notified all staff members to be informed (29th Dispatch).

(Nanjing) The military unification case proposed by Yu Youren and Sun Ke was discussed at the Central Political Conference for a long time and a considerable decision has been made. The principles are related to military affairs and are not convenient to announce (29th Dispatch).

(Nanjing) Wang Jingwei said that the issue of the President of the Executive Yuan was brought up for discussion at the Central Political Conference today. The members advocated for his resumption of duty. Although he repeatedly declined, he could not insist because the members were determined not to allow it. He agreed to continue to maintain his position. After the Standing Committee approves it on the 30th, he will immediately go to the Executive Yuan to resume his duties. He originally intended to return to the country and go north to comfort the troops, but because his illness had not healed and because of the issue of the President of the Executive Yuan, all parties wanted him to resume his duties. Therefore, he will not be able to make the trip in the near future. After his illness has slightly healed and the affairs of the Executive Yuan are slightly sorted out, he will make the trip. In recent days, he has repeatedly received telegrams from Minister He and others, reporting that our army has repeatedly defeated the enemy's vanguard in the anti-Japanese war, so although he did not go, he was very pleased. However, in foreign operations, the whole country must unite and unite to strive for success in order to achieve the most victorious goal. As for the military expenses of the various armies in North China, he intends to discuss a plan with Chairman Chiang to stabilize the morale of the military and to not commit any offenses against the people, so that the cooperation between the military and the people will yield great benefits. The case of opening up the political power proposed by Committee Member Li Liejun was unanimously resolved by the members to be submitted to the Standing Committee on the 30th for discussion. The principles of this case are the same as those of the National Political Participation Council, that is, to implement the Premier's Three Principles of the People, so that the people of the whole country can participate in politics to promote the prelude to constitutional government and implement the foundation of democratic politics. Therefore, all members of the Central Committee expressed their approval. There will be a great discussion at the Standing Committee tomorrow. In order to concentrate the anti-Japanese forces, the Central Committee invited Comrade Feng Huanzhang to come to Nanjing to discuss major plans, but according to his telegram reply, it is temporarily inconvenient to leave the strongholds, so the date of his southward trip is still undecided. (29th Special Dispatch)

Huang Shaoxiong Arrives in Zhangjiakou 39

Has Met Feng Yuxiang to Convey Greetings from Chiang Kai-shek

(Beiping) The Zhangjiakou Anti-Japanese Society telegraphed on the 29th: Minister of Interior Huang Shaoxiong, accompanied by Xiong Bin, Tao Jun, Men Bingyue, and Hu Jiesan, the head of the 41st Army's office in Beiping, arrived in Zhangjiakou from Beiping on the evening of the 28th. Beiping Red Cross Society

Rescues Wounded Soldiers of Sun Dianying's Army 41

A Total of More Than 800 Rescued

(Beiping) Sun Dianying's troops fought fiercely in the vicinity of Chifeng Weichang for more than ten days. Due to a lack of stretchers, the officers and soldiers who died in battle could not be buried during the fierce fighting and were covered by heavy snow. Many of the wounded were lying in the snow, moaning. These wounded soldiers were shot by the Japanese army and frozen to death in the snow in various places, leaving behind more than 900 bodies. The Beiping Red Cross rescue team went to carry them away. More than 200 severely wounded and more than 600 lightly wounded who could move were rescued, totaling more than 800. The first batch of more than 600 has been transported to Zhangjiakou one after another. The second batch of more than 200 was sent from the front to Guyuan. The army has established a field hospital in Kangzhuang, and they will all arrive soon. The Second Regiment of Liu Yaoting's Brigade suffered the most casualties. Liu Zhenxiu, the battalion commander of the First Battalion, was injured. Zhang Chengu, the battalion commander of the Second Battalion, was killed in action. Diao Songting, the lieutenant colonel adjutant of the Third Battalion, was seriously injured. Zhang Fengwu, the major adjutant, was injured and captured. Wang Qingshan, the mortar company commander, was killed in action. Among the twelve company commanders of the Third Battalion, three were killed and four were injured. (29th Special Dispatch)

Sanshui Line Company

Revised Telegraph Service Contract 42

Clauses Started Being Proofread Yesterday Morning

(Nanjing) Regarding the issue of the revised telegraph service contract for the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific Sanshui Line Company, company representatives Svenson and Aikoffsen have come to Nanjing to discuss and handle the matter. The Ministry of Communications sent Director of Telegraph Administration Yan Renguang, Section Chief Guo Shijing, and others to negotiate with them. As a result, because the contract clauses require translation and comparison in both Chinese and English, and there are still places that need to be re-corrected, proofreading began on the morning of the 29th and did not end until 8:00 p.m. Because the content of the clauses is complex, and every word and phrase must be carefully considered to ensure prudence, it will still need to be proofread several times before it can be completed. The contract is expected to be signed next week. As for the Ministry of Communications taking back the company's power to receive and send telegrams, taking over the Shanghai receiving and sending office, and the company applying for a water line landing permit, the company will fulfill these items after the contract is signed and hand them over separately. (29th Special Dispatch)

Investigate the Tang Yulin Case Separately 43

Shao Hongji Issues Statement

(Tianjin) The National Government sent Shao Hongji and Fang Benren to Beiping to investigate the case of Tang Yulin. Fang arrived in Tianjin on the morning of the 27th and took the evening train to Beiping. Shao took the morning train to Beiping on the 29th. According to Shao, Fang is investigating the military part, and I am investigating the lower-level administration. In fact, when Tang was in charge of Rehe, he forced the people to plant opium, embezzled and perverted the law, and imposed exorbitant taxes and levies. The facts are all there. The Control Yuan, in its capacity, should impeach him. This trip to Beiping for investigation is just to complete the procedures. However, how to adopt disciplinary methods in the future still depends on the Central Government. However, the scope of the investigation is only limited to Tang alone. Shao also said that the Control Yuan has a backlog of impeachment cases from all sides, which is difficult to clear up all at once. Among them, there are too many restrictions on the progress of cases involving political officials. Therefore, only three out of more than twenty cases, including Shi Ying's, have been submitted for disciplinary action. This situation is because politics has not yet been put on the right track and cannot give full play to the spirit of the rule of law. (29th Special Dispatch)

Shandong Province Salt Affairs Situation 46

(Jinan) The Donggang Public Office's salt merchants owed the former Shandong Hong Kong Provincial Bank 360,000 yuan, of which 290,000 yuan has been repaid and deposited in the Bank of China. Today, the provincial government's standing committee resolved to allocate the funds for the following purposes: (1) 30,000 for salt tax police; (2) 150,000 for repairing the Second Grand Road; (3) 50,000 for the provincial library; (4) 50,000 for the civilian factory; (5) 2,000 for the widows and orphans relief association; and the remainder will be allocated to the Jinde Association. The remaining 70,000 yuan owed by Donggang will be exempted and no longer repaid. In addition, the provincial salt surtax was originally 1.7 yuan per dan, but it has been reduced by 7 jiao since April. Qingdao salt currently has a contract with Japan to sell 100,000 tons annually. The salt from Linyi, Langcheng, Feixian, and Yishui counties was originally monopolized by special merchants, but now it has been changed to free transportation and sales. Salt Transport Envoy Li Zidingfan will go to Shanghai on the 29th to report on the salt affairs of the province to Finance Minister Song. (29th Special Dispatch)

Tai'an Yarn Factory Shut Down 53

(Hankou) The Tai'an Yarn Factory, operated by Japanese in Hankou, has been shut down since the 27th due to the withdrawal of all Chinese workers. (Hankou) The Japanese-owned Tai'an Yarn Factory recently announced its shutdown because cotton merchants voluntarily refused to sell raw materials, and the yarn factory voluntarily refused to purchase products, making it impossible to continue production. After receiving the report, the garrison command ordered its subordinate military and police organs to pay close attention to protection and maintenance. If there are legitimate issues between labor and management that cannot be resolved, workers should be advised to petition the competent authorities to negotiate or provide relief on their behalf. Direct negotiations are absolutely not allowed, and it is not allowed to stay in the factory or cause trouble and insult. Violators will be arrested without leniency. Czech Envoy Inquires

Truth About Postal Bureau Detaining Parcels 58

(Nanjing) The Czech envoy in Shanghai wrote to the Postal Bureau stating that parcels sent by overseas Chinese in Europe and the United States to eastern provinces are not only not forwarded when they pass through Shanghai, but are often detained. Please investigate and release them quickly. After investigation by the General Post Office, there are currently a total of 84 parcels sent from Europe to overseas Chinese in eastern provinces stored in the bureau. All of them have been issued with non-delivery slips. Currently, 56 parcels have not been answered by the senders, and 12 parcels have been answered and cannot be processed. There are 12 parcels that requested to be sent to Dalian but did not pay import duties and cannot be sent. These are the reasons for the delay. Moreover, our country suspended postal services in the eastern provinces, and on July 23 last year, a telegram was sent to the International Postal Bureau to notify postal administrations of other countries. However, various countries still send parcels to various parts of the three eastern provinces, which cannot be forwarded on our behalf. Parcels sent to Dalian or the South Manchurian Railway area must be handled in accordance with the new customs regulations. Import duties must be paid in Shanghai before they can be sent. The above-mentioned parcels cannot be forwarded because import duties cannot be paid. The Czech envoy stated in the letter that the detention occurred because he did not understand the postal bureau's handling procedures, resulting in a misunderstanding. (29th Special Dispatch)

Jurisdiction of Military Organs 59

(Nanjing) In order to prevent abuses in the trial of military offenders by various military organs, the Ministry of Military Affairs has formulated several points for attention and issued them to various troops for compliance: (1) Troops and military organs that have not stipulated the establishment of military judicial personnel in accordance with the current army organization system are not allowed to try cases; (2) Cases must be tried in accordance with the Army, Navy, and Air Force Trial Law, and the judgment and litigation documents must be sent to the Ministry for approval before they can be executed; (3) Cases involving non-military personnel shall not be accepted unless jurisdiction is authorized by law; (4) The highest military commanders stationed in various places must report to the Ministry for approval as soon as possible in accordance with the Martial Law Regulations if they must temporarily declare martial law. (29th Special Dispatch)

Public Telegram 85

(Telegram from Fang County) To all newspaper offices: Calamity has befallen Southern Henan, with bandits and drought arriving one after the other, burning, looting, and turning homes into ruins. The people have no food or clothing, exposed to the elements, with death on the roads, wailing to the heavens. Recently, even tree bark and grass roots are unattainable. The tragic situation is unprecedented. The spring plowing season is approaching. If farming is abandoned, the consequences are unimaginable. Although headquarters and the Henan Provincial Government have issued relief funds, they are a drop in the bucket. I implore you to have compassion for those who are hungry and drowning, and to show mercy to the suffering people, generously providing relief to benefit the disaster victims, preserve the remnants after the calamity, and save the nation's vitality. Respectfully telegraphing for instructions, I beseech your consideration. The First Administrative Meeting of the Ninth District Administrative Inspectorate of Henan respectfully bows.

Simon Goes to British Parliament

Reports on the Future of the Disarmament Conference 86

British Proposal Offers Hope for a Treaty

Reuter, London, 28th: British Foreign Secretary Simon arrived in London by plane from Geneva this morning to attend the House of Commons and report on the current status of the Disarmament Conference. He stated that the General Committee had unanimously decided yesterday to use the draft treaty proposed by Britain as the basis for future discussions, while the representatives of all countries reserved the right to propose amendments and modifications. The Disarmament Conference will adjourn until April 25th, after which it will study the treaty chapter by chapter and article by article. The British initiative adopted a new approach, placing a broad plan in the form of a treaty before the Disarmament Conference so that each issue could be studied in comparison with other necessary issues. Therefore, the general public has expressed satisfaction with the British proposal, believing it offers the most promising prospect of reaching an agreement.

Hitler Party Leadership

Carries out an Anti-Jewish Movement Throughout Germany 87

Picketers Warn the Public Not to Associate with Jews

The National Socialist Party Announces This Move as Retaliation

Reuter, Berlin, 28th: The National Socialist Party announced today a universal boycott of all Jewish occupations. The government is doing this to retaliate against the overseas scheme to eliminate Jews and exclude Germans. The boycott in Germany is scheduled to begin at 10:00 AM on April 1st and will be carried out by boycott committees throughout the country. These committees will be responsible for monitoring offenders and punishing them, and will be responsible for protecting the personal freedom of foreigners, regardless of their race or nationality. The boycott will be publicized to the public, and German families will not subscribe to newspapers that do not participate in the boycott movement. German stores are not allowed to place advertisements in such newspapers. The anti-Jewish boycott committee must also be responsible for investigating German citizens who have deposits abroad and should use these funds to publicize the truth that Germany is currently very peaceful domestically. The committee must strictly limit the number of Jews who can enter institutions of higher learning or serve as medical and legal professionals, so that their total number has a certain ratio to the total German population. The declaration stated that the boycott should be carried out in a normal and peaceful manner and should not harm a single hair on any Jew's head. The declaration severely condemned the Jews, referring to them as believers in Marxism and blaming Germany for not cracking down on immigration in the past fifteen years, which resulted in a small number of Jewish writers, university professors, and businessmen repaying kindness with ingratitude and inciting the world against the German people, etc. Several towns in Germany have already begun boycotting Jewish businesses. Stormtroopers of the National Socialist Party have been sent out to order Jewish stores to close. Jewish lawyers and doctors in the Glokau area have been forced to cease operations. Shops opened by Jews in the town of Gleiwitz in Upper Silesia are guarded by picketers from the National Socialist Party, and anyone who wants to enter the store to shop is prevented, so although the shops are open, there is no business all day long.

National News, Berlin, 28th: The National Socialist Party stated that German Jews have spread slanderous false information abroad. As retaliation, a national economic boycott will be implemented starting on Saturday. Leaders of the National Socialist Party claimed that they were very angry about the way these people fabricated messages about physical abuse, etc., and broadcast them abroad. Almost all the reports sent by Jews to the United States are fabricated. Only an economic boycott of the Jews can stop them from wantonly slandering. However, the communique issued by the National Socialist Party is not in the form of an ultimatum, so it is believed that if Jewish organizations can guarantee that such messages will not be broadcast abroad in the future, the National Socialist Party may be able to end the economic boycott.

Einstein Vows Not to Return to Germany 88

Opposes the German Government's Deprivation of Citizens' Freedom of Thought

Reuter, Antwerp, 29th: Albert Einstein, the famous Jewish scientist who invented the theory of relativity, arrived here from New York today. The Mayor of Antwerp, a delegation of professors from Belgian and Dutch universities, and the Chairman of the Belgian Jewish Federation all welcomed him at the port. Einstein declared that he would not return to Germany as long as the German government deprives citizens of their freedom of thought. He plans to stay on the Belgian coast for five months.

Japan Ships Large Quantities of Gold Bullion to the United States 89

Reuter, Kobe, 29th: The Japanese government yesterday shipped gold bullion worth 12 million Japanese yen to the United States.

Campaign to Raise the Price of Silver 90

Roosevelt Also Emphasizes

National News, Washington, 28th: Subcommittee Chairman Adams stated today that there is a compromise silver bill that proposes that the government purchase 500 million ounces of domestically produced silver as collateral for issuing silver certificates, that is, using the silver certificates issued to purchase the silver. He will redraft the provisions of this bill in his capacity as chairman and submit it to both houses of Congress immediately. It is expected that this bill will not disrupt the gold standard because the silver certificates issued are guaranteed by silver at market prices. In other words, each silver certificate is guaranteed by about four ounces of silver. Also, government budgets and social finance will not be affected by the purchase of silver, but the silver mining industry will receive tangible relief, and it is not impossible to increase foreign trade, because the purpose of this measure is to raise the price of silver. As for the silver bill proposed by Senator Wheeler at a ratio of sixteen to one, it is inevitable that the price of silver will be falsely set, and he cannot agree with it. He also said that this bill includes the essence of several silver bills in Congress and makes it a circulating medium based on the real price of silver. Only those who sell silver to the government have a speculative nature. If the price of silver falls in the future, these people will suffer losses, but since the purpose of this bill is to raise the price of silver, these people should not suffer losses. The proposers of this bill hope that it will be passed in this Congress. If it is adopted, it may not be necessary to force an international conference to agree on concrete actions to deal with the silver problem.

US-Philippines Wireless Telephone 91

National News, Washington, 28th: Wireless telephone service between the United States and the Philippines will begin on Friday morning. The American transmitting station is in Bolinas, near San Francisco, from where it connects to the national wired telephone network. In addition, wireless telephone service between the Philippines and Germany was also opened earlier this month.

Japanese Military Headquarters Focus on Lengkou 92

Troops Have Been Continuously Reinforced for the Attack

Shang Zhen Also Personally Went to the Front Line to Inspect

Beijing Correspondence: According to a telegram from Kaiping, (1) According to a secret report, the headquarters of the Japanese Kwantung Army has decided to occupy all the passes of the Great Wall, and Lengkou, located in the recessed part of the Great Wall among the six major passes, is particularly important. If Lengkou is occupied, it will not only directly threaten the flanks of the various armies east of the Luan River, but the Chinese troops near the passes to the west will also have to retreat. Therefore, the Okamura 40th Regiment of the Nakamura Mixed Brigade of the 10th Division, the Tani 5th Infantry Regiment of the Suzuki Brigade of the 8th Division, the Taniguchi 1st Artillery Regiment, the Kawada Cavalry Regiment, and part of the Hattori Mixed Brigade drawn from Xifengkou, and part of the West 8th Division have been dispatched to launch a fierce attack on Lengkou from various routes, aiming to capture Lengkou in a short period of time. Currently, various units of the enemy army have gradually come into contact with our army. (2) Since the morning of the 24th, the enemy has continued to use armored vehicles to cover infantry attacks on our Xiaojiaying Madaogou positions, which have been extremely fierce. At the same time, aircraft were used to repeatedly bomb the positions. Our officers and soldiers vowed to resist to the death, killing many enemies. We also suffered casualties of more than ten officers and more than two hundred soldiers. (3) A certain unit that detoured towards a certain place suddenly attacked the enemy's rear around 2:00 AM on the 24th, using hand grenades and broadswords to strike the enemy fiercely. The enemy was unable to resist and retreated slightly. Two armored vehicles were captured and dozens of prisoners were taken. (4) After two days of ineffective attacks, the enemy's infantry was quite silent after the afternoon of the 24th, in addition to using aircraft and artillery fire to fiercely attack our positions. (5) Because enemy planes bombed repeatedly for days, our officers and soldiers suffered heavy casualties, resulting in a shortage of vehicles and materials for transporting the wounded. However, most of those with minor injuries returned to their positions on their own after emergency surgery to continue killing the enemy and did not want to be transported to hospitals in the rear. Shang Zhen, Commander-in-Chief of the 囗 Corps, reported by telegram from the front line to Beijing, Telegram 1, "Lengkou Battle Report (1) I went to inspect the high ground front line in the Madaogou area today and gave instructions to the officers. (2) The morale of the officers and soldiers on the front line is very high. Although they have been fighting for days and suffered heavy casualties, their determination to kill the enemy and serve the country has increased. Division Commander Huang Guanghua, and Regimental Commanders Lin Zuozhen, Jiang Jike, and Lin Jialin are particularly excited and motivated. The work of constructing fortifications near the Great Wall is extremely solid. (3) The front line was quite silent today. Only four aircraft in formation dropped more than twenty bombs over the positions, and artillery fired dozens of shells at our positions. Our losses were minimal. Shang Zhen bows. Unsealed." Telegram 2, "At 2:00 AM this morning, 囗 Division 囗 Regimental Commander personally led the 囗 Battalion of the regiment from the high ground northeast of Madaogou to attack the enemy's rear at Fenghuangzi in Xiaojiaying. At that time, the enemy was extremely panicked, surrounded on all sides. After a fierce battle of about two hours, our 囗 Battalion Commander Zhang Kexun bravely rushed into the enemy's formation first, and the officers and soldiers of the battalion followed, shouting thunderously, killing countless enemies. Battalion Commander Zhang also died in battle in that area, and more than thirty soldiers were wounded or killed. At the same time, a unit of the enemy attacked our Madaogou Chen Di from the Mountain God Temple and was repulsed by our officers and soldiers. More than a hundred enemy corpses were abandoned in the mountain gully this morning. The enemy side is quite shaken and seems to be retreating. Shang Zhen bows. Afternoon seal."

Li Haiqing's Troops

Fierce Battle After Arriving in Rehe 94

Many Enemies Killed and Captured in Kailu

Unfortunately, the Attack Was Foiled by Cui Brigade's Surprise Attack

Now Fighting Back Jointly with Sun Dianying's Army

Ping News: A certain officer of Li Haiqing's Northeast Volunteer Army arrived in Ping yesterday from the battlefield. According to him, "Our army coordinated with Su Bingwen's army last year to attack the capital of Heilongjiang Province. After the defeats at Zhalannor and Manchuria, we were running out of ammunition and had no reinforcements, deeply in enemy territory, with increasing pressure. On January 15th of this year, we arrived at the border of Rehe. Due to years of hard fighting, our men and horses were exhausted. We originally planned to rest our soldiers and replenish our weapons and ammunition before launching another counterattack. Unexpectedly, we came into contact with the enemy again immediately after arriving in Kailu and fought repeatedly. The enemy ultimately did not succeed. The battle on February 7th was the most intense, fighting continuously for three days and nights, driving the enemy back to Tongliao, seizing more than a hundred enemy rifles, capturing forty-two puppet soldiers, killing more than thirty Japanese soldiers, and capturing two Japanese flags and various military supplies. At 4:00 PM on the 23rd, more than thirty large enemy trucks, four armored vehicles, and more than two hundred cavalrymen suddenly pushed back our outposts. At this time, our army's position was on the west bank of the Xingmeng Company River, and the outposts were on the east bank. After Commander Liu (Jingyu) led the team to counterattack, the enemy was driven back, four large trucks were captured, four drivers and two Japanese soldiers were captured alive, and one machine gun and several rifles were captured. We continued to pursue until 6:00 PM, when more than thirty large trucks were surrounded in Kongyuan (a large courtyard divided into three small courtyards). On the order of Commander-in-Chief (Li Haiqing), we decided to resolve the situation at 11:00 PM. Because we lacked guns and ammunition, we selected more than sixty daredevils to jump into the courtyard and attack with hand grenades. By 2:00 AM the next morning, we had occupied one of the three courtyards, destroyed eight enemy trucks, and killed more than thirty Japanese soldiers. While we were resolving the situation, Jin Tuanzhang of Cui Xingwu's brigade suddenly led his troops to attack our army's rear, putting us in a situation where we were attacked from both sides, making it difficult to take care of both. As a result, only sixteen of the more than sixty people who jumped into the courtyard escaped. Our army retreated to Balahuoshaomiao to reorganize our forces and prepare for another counterattack, but troops under Cui's brigade guided the enemy to surround our army again. After a fierce battle lasting a day and a night, our army lost two regimental commanders and more than two hundred soldiers. Because we lacked guns and ammunition, we could not hold out for long and retreated to Daqintala, where we discussed resistance with Yao Brigade of Feng Zhanhai's army. We heard from the brigade commander that Feng's main force had retreated two days earlier. At this time, there were no reinforcements, and the enemy was pressing hard, so we resisted once again in Daqintala. Because the enemy's artillery fire was fierce, we retreated to Wudan City. The city was already empty and could not be stayed in, so we rushed to Cone Mountain and contacted Commander-in-Chief Sun (Dianying), who ordered my First Army to join Sun's army and launch a joint counterattack. The rest of the troops gathered at Banzhaita, but because the villages there were sparse and had already been occupied by friendly forces, we gathered in Dolun. We are currently replenishing weapons and ammunition, training soldiers, and waiting for orders to counterattack." (27th)

Local News

Yesterday's Commemoration of the Yellow Flower Mound Martyrs 101

The City Party Headquarters Held a Commemorative Meeting

The Whole City Flew Flags at Half-Mast and Suspended Entertainment

Yesterday was the 22nd anniversary of the martyrdom of the 72 martyrs of Yellow Flower Mound. Representatives from all walks of life held a commemorative meeting at the City Party Headquarters at 10:00 AM. The whole city flew flags at half-mast and suspended entertainment. Government offices operated as usual. The details are recorded below.

City Flags at Half-Mast 102

All shops, companies, factories, and government offices followed the notification from the City Party Headquarters to fly flags at half-mast to express mourning. All amusement venues and movie theaters suspended entertainment. All government offices under the Municipal Government, the City Party Headquarters, the Shanghai County Government, the Seafarers' Special Party Headquarters, the Garrison Headquarters, the Two-Roads Special Party Headquarters, the City Chamber of Commerce, and other government agencies and organizations followed orders to operate as usual during the serious national crisis and held separate commemorative meetings for the martyrs.

Commemoration by All Sectors 103

The entrance of the City Party Headquarters was decorated with a banner reading "Representatives from All Sectors of Shanghai Hold a Commemorative Meeting for the Revolutionary Martyrs." The Public Security Bureau sent police to maintain order. The venue was covered with posters and slogans. The representatives who attended the meeting were as follows: Chen Kecheng of the Municipal Government, Tong Hangbai of the City Party Headquarters, Zhang Mengling and Miao Jingxian of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Zhu Guilin and Yan Wenkai of the Social Affairs Bureau, Qiu Yuanming of the Land Bureau, Wang Zongjian of the Jianghai Customs, Li Wanqing of the Gaoer Branch, He Yuanming of the Accountants' Association, Dai Youyuan of the Jiangsu Association in Shanghai, Chen Peide of the National Salvation Associations, Zhou Xuexiang of the General Labor Union, Cao Lixin of the Wharf Business Office, and representatives from various universities and schools such as Wusong, Jinan, Nanqu, He'an, Junyi, and Peiben, and from labor unions of industries such as cigarettes, water and electricity, stone printing, cotton weaving, cotton spinning, knitting, foundry, and medicine, and from various levels of the Party Headquarters, totaling more than 500 people.

Chairman's Report 104

The meeting was chaired by Tong Hangbai, with Fan Mingyao as the master of ceremonies and Tong Muge as the recorder. After performing the rituals, everyone observed three minutes of silence for the revolutionary martyrs. Then, the chairman reported, "Comrades and compatriots, today we are holding the 22nd anniversary of the commemoration of the 72 martyrs of Yellow Flower Mound. I feel stimulated in spirit, especially during this serious national crisis when the nation's territory has been taken away and the nation's status is extremely dangerous. We should commemorate the glorious deeds of the revolutionary martyrs of the past and continue to implement their unfinished legacy, to recover the lost territories of the Northeast and to eliminate the communist bandits domestically. With the spirit of struggle and sacrifice of the martyrs, and with the determination for long-term resistance, then even if the violent enemy is strong, they will eventually succumb. We should (1) recognize that the martyrs were young people with aspirations, the pillars of the nation, and their sacrifice is the nation's greatest loss. (2) Recognize that the revolutionary actions of the martyrs were inspired by the Three Principles of the People, giving rise to national spirit and creating glorious deeds. (3) Recognize that the success of the Xinhai Revolution was due to the determination of the past ten revolutions, unified solidarity, and facing the national crisis together. Then there will be a day when our lost territories in the Northeast will be recovered and national humiliation can be washed away." The meeting adjourned at 12:00 PM.

Oral Slogans 105

Slogans: (1) March 29th is the day revolutionary martyrs died for their country; (2) The revolutionary martyrs of March 29th were faithful believers in the Three Principles of the People; (3) To commemorate the revolutionary martyrs, we must resist the violent Japanese; (4) To commemorate the revolutionary martyrs, we must work hard on national construction; (5) To commemorate the revolutionary martyrs, we must eliminate the communist bandits; (6) The spirit of the revolutionary martyrs is immortal; (7) Long live the Three Principles of the People; (8) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party; (9) Long live the Republic of China. Slogans: (1) Urge the government to recover the lost territory of the Northeast; (2) Continue the spirit of the martyrs and economically sever ties with Japan; (3) Commemorate the unfinished legacy of the revolutionary martyrs; (4) March 29th is one of the most glorious pages in revolutionary history.

T.V. Soong Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning

No Problem with President Wang's Resumption of Office 109

Expiration and Abolition of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement

Unification of the Monetary System and Consolidation of Various Tax Revenues

Vice President of the Executive Yuan, T.V. Soong, left Nanjing by night express train the night before last and returned to Shanghai at about 8:00 yesterday morning. Reporters from various newspapers went to visit Mr. Soong at his private residence. According to his statement, the issue of Wang Jingwei returning to his position as President of the Executive Yuan will be formally resumed after a decision is made at this morning's Central Political Conference. The details of Mr. Soong's statement are recorded below.

Wang to Resume Office Soon 110

Mr. Soong indicated that there is absolutely no problem with Mr. Wang returning to his position as President of the Executive Yuan. The resumption of office will be implemented after the Central Political Conference decides this morning. He will be fully responsible for all political affairs hereafter, while he will specialize in financial matters. Therefore, what I can discuss with you at the moment is limited to financial matters. Although I still concurrently serve as Vice President of the Executive Yuan, the Vice President has no right to make statements related to the Executive Yuan.

News of Chiang's Arrival in Shanghai 111

The reporter then inquired whether the news of Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission Chiang Kai-shek's upcoming visit to Shanghai was accurate. Mr. Soong did not give a definitive answer, only saying that he had seen this record in the newspapers, but he did not deny it either. It is said that Chiang will come to Shanghai within a day or two after attending today's Central Political Conference.

Unify Subsidiary Currency 112

Mr. Soong also said that various commercial groups have requested the unification of subsidiary currency, and this matter can be done. In addition to copper and silver subsidiary currency, there is currently no nickel currency in our country. Nickel currency is more difficult to imitate. Most countries often use this nickel currency to transform into military supplies, such as bullets, etc., in times of emergency. The supply of raw materials is difficult. As for the implementation of the gold standard, it is also difficult, because countries that implement the gold standard buy silver with gold more cheaply, while countries that do not implement the gold standard find it extremely difficult to buy gold with silver. Whether the World Economic Conference will be held in May has not yet been decided, so whether I will go to Europe to attend is also not yet scheduled.

Tariff Agreement 113

The Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement will expire and become invalid after May 16th. There is no question of renewal. The agreement only stipulates that the import tax on certain goods will be maintained for one and three years respectively. Initially, because our country concluded agreements with various countries on tariff autonomy, Japan could not be an exception. Therefore, the minimum tax rate was maintained, hence this provision.

Consolidate Tax Revenue 114

Regarding the consolidation of tax revenue, the North China region has already been returned to the Central Government, and there is no problem in the South China region either. Soong explained that the unification of tax revenue does not mean that tax revenue is unified only when the Central Government sends people to handle tax collection. Rather, it means that any method that can be handled in accordance with the Central Government's methods is considered unified. Therefore, the Central Government seeks to simplify the consolidation of tax revenue. As for the consolidation of salt tax, it is also better at this time than before.

China National Aviation Corporation

Newly Purchased Aircraft Arrives in Shanghai 119

Currently Verifying Postal Rate Standards with the Post Office

The China National Aviation Corporation's newly purchased Lorraine amphibious aircraft was shipped to Shanghai on the President Pierce liner the day before yesterday. The company immediately extracted it from the customs and temporarily placed it in the warehouse at the Dalei Wharf. Yesterday morning, the company's aviation department sent a technician, Mr. Wirth, to match the fuselage and hire a tugboat to drag it to the Longhua Airport, where the motor and parts will be installed. After a test flight at the airport, it will be put into operation on the Shanghai-Hankou line and has been named "Chongqing." In addition, the company, in order to verify postal rate standards, has sent staff member Cai Guangmo to the post office since the 13th of this month to jointly check the total number of daily mail items, using the average number of two weeks as the standard. The results of the secret inspection show that the previously determined standard of 21 yuan per kilogram for the first zone and 41 yuan per kilogram for the second zone paid by the post office is still fair. Whether it will be revised again remains to be negotiated between the two parties. As for the average number of mail items per day, the first postal zone is 1,681 items, with postal revenue of 420.25 yuan, with the most being sent to Hankou. The second zone has 535 mail items, with postal revenue of 267.50 yuan, with the most being sent to Chongqing. The average daily postal revenue for both zones is about 700 yuan. Although it is not enough to cover expenses, a surplus can be expected if passenger transport increases.

We hope that your company's flight to Dihua will be completed as soon as possible. Moreover, the routes passed are all safe areas, and there will be no hindrance to travel. We urge you to complete it with great effort and determine the schedule. The transportation between Beijing and Dihua will be smooth and convenient, and both public and private sectors will benefit immensely. Dedicated to your honor, respectfully, Zhang Fengjiu.
